## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor rate laws / ODE kinetics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is a time-derivative of concentration, which is the standard object modeled by chemical kinetics ODEs in a batch (or well-mixed) system. With only (t, A) available, plausible models are rate laws where the reaction rate depends on A (reaction order, saturation/inhibition, equilibrium driving force) and possibly explicit time-dependence (time-varying rate constant, forcing, deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or saturated catalyst where rate is independent of A over a range)
- First-order (unimolecular) decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (radioactive-like or unimolecular reaction in batch)
- Second-order (bimolecular in A) decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (2A -> products, or pseudo-second-order cases)
- General nth-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (two simultaneous consumption channels)
- Source-plus-decay (production and loss): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (inflow/generation with first-order removal)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to distance from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating with limitation: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with a limiting concentration/capacity)
- Product (or self) inhibition / site limitation: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate increases with A at low A and saturates at high A due to limited sites)
- Time-varying rate constant (activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective first-order kinetics with k(t) changing exponentially in time)
- Aging or diffusion-limited effective kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (t + c1)**(-c2) (rate slows down over time due to deactivation, diffusion layers, or depletion effects)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * A (rate modulated by periodic temperature/light/input variations)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption of A typically implies dA_dt <= 0 for A >= 0; sign flips or positive dA_dt suggest production terms or reversibility toward an equilibrium level.
- If dA_dt scales linearly with A near A ≈ 0, it indicates unimolecular/pseudo-first-order behavior; if it scales like A**2, it suggests bimolecular dependence on A.
- A driving-force form (A - c_eq) indicates relaxation toward a steady state/equilibrium concentration c_eq where the net rate vanishes.
- Autocatalytic structure A*(c - A) implies an initially accelerating rate (as A grows) followed by slowdown near a capacity/limiting level c.
- Rational saturation in A (e.g., A/(c + A)) indicates limited active sites or inhibition/competition causing diminishing returns at high A.
- Explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient (e.g., exp(c*t), (t+c)**(-p), sin(c*t)) often represents changing conditions: catalyst deactivation/activation, diffusion boundary layer growth, or external forcing.
- A sum of multiple A-dependent terms (e.g., -c*A - c*A**2) suggests parallel mechanisms or regime superposition rather than a single elementary step.
- Physical feasibility often requires A(t) >= 0; good rate-law candidates tend to satisfy dA_dt -> 0 as A -> 0 for pure-consumption mechanisms (no source term).

GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_f*A**c4
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is:
\[
F(t,A)=0.7991114344496316\,A^{1/3}-0.4994732695791710\,A-0.4994732695791710\,A\,e^{-0.050569865727257013\,t}.
\]
Key structural facts:
- Only three terms: \(A^{1/3}\), \(A\), and \(A e^{kt}\) with \(k<0\).
- No rational-in-\(A\) terms like \(\frac{1}{A+\cdot}\) or \(\frac{t}{A+\cdot}\), no extra constants, no trig/log.
- The exponential term is exactly proportional to \(A\) (not divided by \(A+\cdot\), etc.).

Now check candidates.

1) \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}c4 + A^{c5} + \frac{c6 t}{A c7+c8} + \frac{1}{A c7+c8}\).  
Can set \(c6=0\) to remove \(t/(...)\), but \(\frac{1}{A c7+c8}\) cannot be removed unless you force it to be identically 0, which is impossible (no multiplicative free coefficient). So cannot match GT.

2) Has \(+A\), \(+c8\), and \(t/(A+c8)\) term. You can’t remove the standalone \(+A\) (fixed coefficient 1). So no.

3) \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3 + A^{c4} + c5 + c6 t/(A+c7)\).  
You can set \(c6=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then you have \(A\) terms (combine \(c0+c3\)), one \(A^{c4}\), and one \(A e^{c2 t}\). This *could* match GT by choosing:
- \(c4=1/3\) and coefficient 0.799111...,
- \(c2=-0.0505698657\),
- \(c1=-0.4994732696\),
- \(c0+c3=-0.4994732696\).
Yes, this matches exactly (no extra unavoidable terms). ✅

4) Includes \(c4 t/(A+c5)+1/(A+c5)\) with unavoidable \(1/(A+c5)\). Cannot match.

5) Can set \(c7=0\) to remove \(t/(A+c8)\). Remaining: \(A(c0+c3)+A c1 e^{c2 t}+A^{c4}+A^{c5}c6\). To match GT you’d need only one power term \(A^{1/3}\); you can set one of the power-term coefficients to 0 by setting \(c6=0\), and set the other exponent \(c4=1/3\). Then it reduces to same matchable structure as (3). ✅

6) Has \(c7 t/(A c3+c8)+c8\). You can set \(c7=0\) but the standalone \(+c8\) must be 0; that’s fine by setting \(c8=0\). However denominator becomes \(A c3\) and term is gone anyway. Remaining includes \(A^{c6}\) plus \(A^{c4}c5\) plus linear and exp. You can kill one power term by setting its coefficient 0 (set \(c5=0\) or choose exponent and coefficient to make it redundant). But there is also \(A*c3\) and \(A*c0\) and \(A*c1 e^{c2 t}\): structurally matchable. Yet note \(c3\) appears both as linear coefficient and inside the removed denominator; since denominator term removed, no constraint. So yes: set \(c7=0,c8=0\); set one power term coefficient 0; set the other to \(A^{1/3}\) with correct coefficient; set exp rate negative and coefficients to match. ✅

7) Has \(+1/(A+c8)\) unavoidable (no coefficient). Cannot match.

8) Has \(+c8 + 1/(A+c7)\) unavoidable unless impossible; you can set \(c8=0\) but not remove \(1/(A+c7)\). No.

9) Polynomial/rational mix with \(A^3,A^2\), terms divided by \(A+c3\), plus standalone \(c7\), plus exp terms not purely \(A e^{kt}\). Cannot reduce to GT’s simple 3-term form (unavoidable rational structure). No.

10) Has \(+1/(A*c5+c6)\) unavoidable. No.

11) Has \(+1/(A+c6)\) unavoidable. No.

12) Has \(c7/(A*c5+c6)\) which can be removed by \(c7=0\), and \(c4 t/(...)\) removable by \(c4=0\). Then it becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}\), which can match GT by setting \(c3=1/3\) and choosing \(c0,c1,c2\) appropriately **but GT also has an extra linear \(-0.499...A\)** in addition to the exp-linear term. Here linear term is only \(A c0\), so set \(c0=-0.499473...\) and \(c1=-0.499473...\), \(c2=-0.05056...\), and set \(A^{c3}\) coefficient? Wait candidate 12 has \(+A^{c3}\) with implicit coefficient 1 (no multiplier). That forces coefficient of \(A^{c3}\) to be 1, but GT’s coefficient is 0.799111... So cannot match. No.

13)–29) These are all built from \(A^3, A^2\), and/or rational terms \(\frac{\cdot}{A+c}\), plus exp terms often divided by \(A+c\), plus extra constants. GT has none of these rational structures. You generally cannot eliminate \(\frac{A}{A+c}\), \(\frac{1}{A+c}\), etc. unless their numerators’ coefficients are forced to 0; but many such terms have fixed numerator like \(A/(A+c)\) with coefficient 1 (unremovable). Therefore none of 13–29 can match. (Examples: 13 has \(A/(A+c4)\) with coefficient 1; 23 has \(A/(A+c3)\) with coefficient 1; 27 has \(\frac{A c2}{A+c3}\) etc. Even if you set some coefficients 0, the fixed \(A/(A+c)\) terms remain.)

30) Contains \(c6 t/(A*c7+c8)\) removable by \(c6=0\), but also \(1/(A+c8)\) unavoidable. No.

31) \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3 e^{c4 t} + A c5 + A^{c6} + c7\).  
To match GT you must remove extra exp term \(A c3 e^{c4 t}\) by setting \(c3=0\), remove constant \(c7=0\), then you have \(A(c0+c5)+A c1 e^{c2 t}+A^{c6}\). This matches GT by choosing \(c6=1/3\), \(c2=-0.05056...\), \(c1=-0.49947...\), \(c0+c5=-0.49947...\), and coefficient of \(A^{c6}\) is 1 (implicit!)—actually here \(A^{c6}\) has implicit coefficient 1, so it would force \(0.799111...=1\), impossible. No.

32) Has many \((A+c0)\) denominators and unavoidable \(1/(A+c0)\). No.

33) Has \(1/(A+c3)\) unavoidable. No.

34) Has sine term and logistic-like \(c7/(c8 e^{c9 t}+1)\); can set their coefficients 0 (c4=0,c7=0). Then becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}\) with implicit coefficient 1 on \(A^{c3}\), again cannot match 0.799111... unless 0.799111...=1. No.

35) Has \(c6/A\) unavoidable unless \(c6=0\) (ok), but still has all terms divided by \(A+c1\) so yields rational dependence not in GT unless you force \(c1=0\) and then terms become divided by \(A\) etc; still not matchable to pure \(A\) and \(A^{1/3}\) without denominators. No.

36) Contains terms with \(/(A+c1)\) and also \(A c2\) (ok) but the rational terms cannot all be removed (some have fixed structure). No.

37) Has extra \(c4 e^{c5 t}\) removable by \(c4=0\) and sine removable by \(c6=0\). Then becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}\) with implicit coefficient 1 on \(A^{c3}\) → cannot match 0.799111... No.

38) Has cosine term removable by setting \(c5=0\) (since it multiplies), and rational \(c7/(A c8+c9)\) removable by \(c7=0\). Then becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}\) with implicit coefficient 1 on \(A^{c3}\) → cannot match. No.

40) Has \(A/(A+c3)\) with coefficient 1; cannot match. No.

42) Has \(c4/(A c5+c6)\) removable by \(c4=0\). Then becomes \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}\) with implicit coefficient 1 on \(A^{c3}\) → cannot match. No.

43) Has logs; cannot remove unless coefficients 0, but then left with \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3/(A+c4)\) which is rational in \(A\) unless \(c3=0\). Then reduces to \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\) missing \(A^{1/3}\). No.
